**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

    First Check After Step 5

    First Check After Step 6

    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

Federal Agency Restructuring & White House Communications  
President Trump has initiated efforts to reclassify federal workers, making it easier to terminate their employment [1]. The Department of Defense is experiencing leadership upheaval, with Secretary Hegseth removing four staffers in a single day [2]. FEMA budget cuts are directly impacting water infrastructure projects in Portsmouth and Richmond [3].

The White House faces scrutiny over multiple communications issues. Covid.gov has been replaced with content promoting lab leak theories about COVID-19's origins [4]. A letter to Harvard containing demands was later claimed by the White House to be an "unauthorized mistake" [5]. Other notable communications include posting photos of the president with actor Vince Vaughn [6] and sharing an image of deported individual Kilmar Abrego Garcia that allegedly contained a photoshopped MS-13 gang tattoo [7].

A DOGE representative has reportedly verbally abused federal workers on a 36-hour shift [8], though limited information is available about broader DOGE operations.

Supreme Court and Legal Challenges  
The Supreme Court has issued a temporary restraining order blocking the Trump administration from deporting Venezuelan migrants under the Alien Enemies Act, a rarely-used wartime law [1]. The administration responded by characterizing the litigation as "meritless" [2]. The Court is also set to hear challenges to the Affordable Care Act's preventive care mandate [3] and arguments on Trump's attempt to ignore the 14th Amendment regarding birthright citizenship [4].

Justice Department policies under Attorney General Pam Bondi include severe penalties for Tesla vehicle vandalism, with promises of "decades behind bars" for perpetrators [5]. Simultaneously, the judiciary is pushing back on detention practices, with a federal judge ordering Rumeysa Ozturk's transfer from Louisiana to Vermont, explicitly stating that "the government cannot undermine the justice system and attempt to manipulate a case's jurisdiction" [6].

A conservative judge in the Kilmar Abrego Garcia case has issued what is described as a "wake up call for America," warning of imminent threats to democracy [7].

OPPOSITION & PUBLIC RESPONSE

Protest Movements and Political Dissent  
A significant nationwide protest movement known as "50501" has emerged, with demonstrators rallying in major cities for a second consecutive weekend [1]. The protests focus on deportation policies, due process rights [2], and other administration actions including DOGE operations and tariffs, using the slogan "Hands Off!" [3].

Fissures within Republican ranks are becoming increasingly visible. An Associated Press report highlights how pardoned January 6 rioters are being embraced within Republican politics [4]. Michigan Representative Thanedar has called for Trump's impeachment over the Kilmar Abrego Garcia case [5]. Conservative activist Charlie Kirk has publicly split with Trump over the antisemitism crackdown, expressing concerns about potential threats to free speech rights [6].

Trump's approval rating on the economy has dropped to the lowest point of his presidential career [7]. Former Trump staff members have harshly criticized the president's leadership style, comparing his actions to those of a "Royal Despot" [8]. Republican lawmakers have reportedly encountered angry constituents at public events, with some situations escalating to the point where tasers were deployed [9].

IMMIGRATION & DEPORTATION POLICIES

Border Security and High-Profile Cases  
Border security measures have intensified to the point where U.S. citizens are reportedly being detained when returning from Canada [1]. The Trump administration has reportedly removed a U.S. citizen from Social Security benefits as part of what is characterized as an "Anti-Immigrant Purge" [2].

Several high-profile deportation cases have drawn significant attention. Maryland Senator Hollen has had a face-to-face meeting with a man described as "mistakenly deported" [3] and has accused El Salvador of staging a photo opportunity with a wrongfully deported U.S. resident, claiming the Trump administration is defying court orders to return the individual [4].

The administration has cited potential threats to Middle East peace process negotiations as justification for deporting Mohsen Mahdawi, a student who led Columbia University protests, according to a memo from Secretary of State Marco Rubio [5]. An Indonesian student has reportedly been detained by Immigration and Customs Enforcement after the U.S. "secretly revoked his visa" [6].

ECONOMIC POLICY & SOCIAL ISSUES

Tariffs and Trade Impacts  
The administration's tariff policies are generating significant economic consequences. Volvo is cutting up to 800 U.S. jobs due to tariff uncertainty [1], while economists warn of imminent "shockwaves" to the world economy [2]. A group of top economists has circulated a letter stating that Trump's tariffs have "no basis in economic reality" [3]. Corporate leadership has been notably silent, with this lack of protest characterized as "one of the biggest failures of leadership in corporate history" [4]. Consumer goods are being impacted, with bananas described as "the next victim" after eggs [5].

Academic Freedom and Healthcare  
Academic institutions are facing significant pressure from the administration. Harvard University has refused to comply with government demands [1], characterizing them as "astonishing overreach" [2]. The Department of Justice has claimed that academic journals hold "partisan" stances in scientific debates [3], while New Jersey's schools department has rejected the administration's demands to eliminate diversity, equity, and inclusion programs [4].

Healthcare systems appear to be facing challenges under current policies. A New Yorker investigation has raised concerns about incarcerated people dying from lack of food or water while private companies continue to receive millions for their care [5]. Trump's aid cuts are reportedly affecting hungry populations in "a city of shellfire and starvation" [6]. A law firm claims that the CDC and FDA have been "gutted" to the point where they are not issuing warnings about a farm associated with a deadly 2024 E. coli outbreak [7].

The Environmental Protection Agency has reportedly deleted pollution tracking tools while simultaneously offering exemptions to polluters [8].

EXECUTIVE BRANCH ACTIONS & JUDICIAL RESPONSE

Federal Agency Restructuring & White House Communications  
President Trump has initiated efforts to reclassify federal workers, making it easier to terminate their employment [1]. The Department of Defense is experiencing leadership upheaval, with Secretary Hegseth removing four staffers in a single day [2]. FEMA budget cuts are directly impacting water infrastructure projects in Portsmouth and Richmond [3].

The White House faces scrutiny over multiple communications issues. Covid.gov has been replaced with content promoting lab leak theories about COVID-19's origins [4]. A letter to Harvard containing demands was later claimed by the White House to be an "unauthorized mistake" [5]. Other notable communications include posting photos of the president with actor Vince Vaughn [6] and sharing an image of deported individual Kilmar Abrego Garcia that allegedly contained a photoshopped MS-13 gang tattoo [7].

A DOGE representative has reportedly verbally abused federal workers on a 36-hour shift [8], though limited information is available about broader DOGE operations.

Supreme Court and Legal Challenges  
The Supreme Court has issued a temporary restraining order blocking the Trump administration from deporting Venezuelan migrants under the Alien Enemies Act, a rarely-used wartime law [1]. The administration responded by characterizing the litigation as "meritless" [2]. The Court is also set to hear challenges to the Affordable Care Act's preventive care mandate [3] and arguments on Trump's attempt to ignore the 14th Amendment regarding birthright citizenship [4].

Justice Department policies under Attorney General Pam Bondi include severe penalties for Tesla vehicle vandalism, with promises of "decades behind bars" for perpetrators [5]. Simultaneously, the judiciary is pushing back on detention practices, with a federal judge ordering Rumeysa Ozturk's transfer from Louisiana to Vermont, explicitly stating that "the government cannot undermine the justice system and attempt to manipulate a case's jurisdiction" [6].

A conservative judge in the Kilmar Abrego Garcia case has issued what is described as a "wake up call for America," warning of imminent threats to democracy [7].

[1] US Supreme Court temporarily blocks deportations of Venezuelan migrants under wartime law, https://www.reuters.com/world/us/us-supreme-court-temporarily-blocks-deportations-venezuelan-migrants-under-2025-04-19/;  
[2] After remarkable Supreme Court rebuke, Trump administration slams ‘meritless litigation’, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/04/19/supreme-court-trump-immigration-ruling-00299717;  
[3] Supreme Court to hear challenge to Obamacare rule on free preventive care | The Affordable Care Act requires insurers to cover a range of preventive services, including cancer screenings, statins and HIV-prevention medications., https://www.nbcnews.com/health/health-news/obamacare-supreme-court-preventative-care-challenge-rcna201794;

INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS

Middle East and Global Diplomacy  
U.S. airstrikes on a Houthi-controlled port have resulted in more than 70 casualties, with Yemen's Houthi forces vowing to continue their attacks in response [1]. Simultaneously, Iran and the U.S. have moved to expert-level talks over Tehran’s nuclear program following negotiations in Rome [2].

President Trump has backed away from his campaign promise to end the Russia-Ukraine war within 24 hours of taking office [3]. On the China front, Trump and President Xi Jinping are locked in a diplomatic standoff over direct trade negotiations [4].

Canadian university teachers have been warned against traveling to the United States [5], while Canada experiences record turnout in advance voting for its elections [6]. Vice President Vance has engaged in an "exchange of opinions" with the Vatican regarding immigration policies [7], with Pope Francis reportedly declining to meet personally with Vance, instead sending a deputy who lectured the VP on compassion [8].

OPPOSITION & PUBLIC RESPONSE

Protest Movements and Political Dissent  
A significant nationwide protest movement known as "50501" has emerged, with demonstrators rallying in major cities for a second consecutive weekend [1]. The protests focus on deportation policies, due process rights [2], and other administration actions including DOGE operations and tariffs, using the slogan "Hands Off!" [3].

Fissures within Republican ranks are becoming increasingly visible. An Associated Press report highlights how pardoned January 6 rioters are being embraced within Republican politics [4]. Michigan Representative Thanedar has called for Trump's impeachment over the Kilmar Abrego Garcia case [5]. Conservative activist Charlie Kirk has publicly split with Trump over the antisemitism crackdown, expressing concerns about potential threats to free speech rights [6].

Trump's approval rating on the economy has dropped to the lowest point of his presidential career [7]. Former Trump staff members have harshly criticized the president's leadership style, comparing his actions to those of a "Royal Despot" [8]. Republican lawmakers have reportedly encountered angry constituents at public events, with some situations escalating to the point where tasers were deployed [9].
